/></a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Amy Jade Winehouse</b> (14 September 1983 \xe2\x80\x93 23 July 2011) was an English singer and songwriter. She was known for her deep, expressive <a href="/wiki/Contralto" title="Contralto">contralto</a> vocals and her eclectic mix of musical genres, including <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> (sometimes labelled as <a href="/wiki/Blue-eyed_soul" title="Blue-eyed soul">blue-eyed soul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neo_soul" title="Neo soul">neo soul</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">rhythm and blues</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frank_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frank-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse\'s debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Frank_(Amy_Winehouse_album)" title="Frank (Amy Winehouse album)">Frank</a></i> (2003), was a critical success in the UK and was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Prize" title="Mercury Prize">Mercury Prize</a>. Her follow-up album, <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_Black" title="Back to Black">Back to Black</a></i> (2006), led to five <a href="/wiki/50th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="50th Annual Grammy Awards">2008 Grammy Awards</a>, tying the then <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_records#Most_Grammys_won_by_a_female_artist_in_one_night" title="Grammy Award records">record for the most wins by a female artist in a single night</a>, and made her the first British woman to win five Grammys,<sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> including three of the <a href="/wiki/General_Field_%22Big_Four%22_Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="General Field &quot;Big Four&quot; Grammy Award">General Field "Big Four" Grammy Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/2008_General_Field_%22Big_Four%22_Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 General Field &quot;Big Four&quot; Grammy Award">Best New Artist, Record of the Year and Song of the Year</a>.\n</p><p>Winehouse won three <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Awards" title="Ivor Novello Awards">Ivor Novello Awards</a> from the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers,_and_Authors" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers, and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers, and Authors</a>: in 2004, Best Contemporary Song for "<a href="/wiki/Stronger_Than_Me" title="Stronger Than Me">Stronger Than Me</a>"; in 2007, Best Contemporary Song again, this time for "<a href="/wiki/Rehab_(Amy_Winehouse_song)" title="Rehab (Amy Winehouse song)">Rehab</a>"; and in 2008, Best Song Musically and Lyrically for "<a href="/wiki/Love_Is_a_Losing_Game" title="Love Is a Losing Game">Love Is a Losing Game</a>." She also won the <a href="/wiki/2007_Brit_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="2007 Brit Award">2007 Brit Award</a> for Best British Female Artist, having been nominated for Best British Album, with <i>Back to Black</i>.\n</p><p>Winehouse died of <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_intoxication" title="Alcohol intoxication">alcohol poisoning</a> on 23 July 2011, <a href="/wiki/27_Club" title="27 Club">at the age of 27</a>. Her album <i>Back to Black</i> posthumously became, for a time, the UK\'s best-selling album of the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Artwork_and_Tussauds_wax_figure"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Artwork and Tussauds wax figure</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#The_next_generation"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">The next generation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Amy_Winehouse_Foundation"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Amy Winehouse Foundation</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Films"><span class="tocnumber">9.4</span> <span class="toctext">Films</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Relationships"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Relationships</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Substance_abuse_and_mental_illness"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Substance abuse and mental illness</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Violence_and_legal_difficulties"><span class="tocnumber">10.3</span> <span class="toctext">Violence and legal difficulties</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Paparazzi"><span class="tocnumber">10.4</span> <span class="toctext">Paparazzi</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Respiratory_and_other_health_problems"><span class="tocnumber">10.5</span> <span class="toctext">Respiratory and other health problems</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#Death"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Death</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Posthumous_retrospectives"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Posthumous retrospectives</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Discography"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Discography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Filmography"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Filmography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">17</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>\n<p>Amy Winehouse was born in <a href="/wiki/Chase_Farm_Hospital" title="Chase Farm Hospital">Chase Farm Hospital</a>, in north London, to <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> parents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012xiii_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012xiii-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Her father, Mitchell "Mitch" Winehouse, was a window panel installer<sup id="cite_ref-Mitch_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mitch-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and then a taxi driver; and her mother, Janis Winehouse (n\xc3\xa9e Seaton),<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> was a pharmacist.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse\'s ancestors were <a href="/wiki/Russian_Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Jewish">Russian Jewish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polish_Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Jewish">Polish Jewish</a> immigrants to London. Amy had an older brother, Alex (born 1979),<sup id="cite_ref-DD_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DD-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and the family lived in London\'s <a href="/wiki/Southgate,_London" title="Southgate, London">Southgate</a> area,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012xiii_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012xiii-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> where she attended Osidge Primary School.<sup id="cite_ref-Alex_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alex-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse as a child attended a Jewish Sunday school.<sup id="cite_ref-amyw1_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amyw1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> After she rose to fame, during an interview she expressed her dismissal towards the school by saying that she used to beg her father to allow her not to go and that she learned nothing about being Jewish by going anyway.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In the same interview, Winehouse said she only went to a synagogue once a year on <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur" title="Yom Kippur">Yom Kippur</a> "out of respect".<sup id="cite_ref-amyw1_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amyw1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many of Winehouse\'s maternal uncles were professional jazz musicians.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Amy\'s paternal grandmother, Cynthia, was a singer and dated the English jazz saxophonist <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Scott" title="Ronnie Scott">Ronnie Scott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-C&amp;D_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C&amp;D-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> She and Amy\'s parents influenced Amy\'s interest in jazz.<sup id="cite_ref-C&amp;D_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C&amp;D-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Her father, Mitch, often sang <a href="/wiki/Frank_Sinatra" title="Frank Sinatra">Frank Sinatra</a> songs to her, and whenever she got chastised at school, she would sing "<a href="/wiki/Fly_Me_to_the_Moon" title="Fly Me to the Moon">Fly Me to the Moon</a>" before going up to the headmistress to be told off.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse\'s parents separated when she was nine,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and she lived with her mother and stayed with her father and his girlfriend in <a href="/wiki/Hatfield_Heath" title="Hatfield Heath">Hatfield Heath</a>, Essex, on weekends.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201212_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201212-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1992, her grandmother Cynthia suggested that Amy attend the <a href="/wiki/Susi_Earnshaw_Theatre_School" title="Susi Earnshaw Theatre School">Susi Earnshaw Theatre School</a>, where she went on Saturdays to further her vocal education and to learn to tap dance.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201215_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201215-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> She attended the school for four years and founded a short-lived rap group called Sweet \'n\' Sour, with Juliette Ashby, her childhood friend,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> before seeking full-time training at <a href="/wiki/Sylvia_Young_Theatre_School" title="Sylvia Young Theatre School">Sylvia Young Theatre School</a>. Winehouse was allegedly expelled at 14 for "not applying herself" and also for piercing her nose.<sup id="cite_ref-DD_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DD-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sylvia_Young" title="Sylvia Young">Sylvia Young</a> has denied this\xe2\x80\x94"She changed schools at 15...I\'ve heard it said she was expelled; she wasn\'t. I\'d never have expelled Amy"<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94as has Mitch Winehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-Mitch_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mitch-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> She also appeared in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fast_Show" title="The Fast Show">The Fast Show</a></i>, 1997, with other children from the Sylvia Young School<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and later attended the <a href="/wiki/The_Mount_School,_Mill_Hill" class="mw-redirect" title="The Mount School, Mill Hill">Mount School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mill_Hill" title="Mill Hill">Mill Hill</a>; the <a href="/wiki/BRIT_School" title="BRIT School">BRIT School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Selhurst" title="Selhurst">Selhurst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a>; Osidge JMI School and then <a href="/wiki/Ashmole_Academy" title="Ashmole Academy">Ashmole School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_career">Musical career</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span></h3>\n<p>After toying around with her brother Alex\'s guitar, Winehouse bought her own when she was 14 and began writing music a year later. Soon after, she began working for a living, including, at one time, as an entertainment journalist for the <a href="/wiki/World_Entertainment_News_Network" title="World Entertainment News Network">World Entertainment News Network</a>, in addition to singing with local group the Bolsha Band.<sup id="cite_ref-DD_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DD-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In July 2000, she became the featured female vocalist with the <a href="/wiki/National_Youth_Jazz_Orchestra" title="National Youth Jazz Orchestra">National Youth Jazz Orchestra</a>; her influences were to include <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Vaughan" title="Sarah Vaughan">Sarah Vaughan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dinah_Washington" title="Dinah Washington">Dinah Washington</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> the latter of whom she was already listening to at home.<sup id="cite_ref-C&amp;D_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C&amp;D-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Amy\'s best friend, soul singer <a href="/wiki/Tyler_James_(English_musician)" title="Tyler James (English musician)">Tyler James</a>, sent her demo tape to an <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> person.<sup id="cite_ref-C&amp;D_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C&amp;D-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse signed to <a href="/wiki/Simon_Fuller" title="Simon Fuller">Simon Fuller</a>\'s 19 Management in 2002 and was paid \xc2\xa3250 a week against future earnings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201234_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201234-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> While being developed by the management company, she was kept as a recording industry secret<sup id="cite_ref-HQ_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HQ-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> although she was a regular jazz standards singer at the Cobden Club.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201234_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201234-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Her future A&amp;R representative at <a href="/wiki/Island_(Universal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Island (Universal)">Island</a>, Darcus Beese, heard of her by accident when the manager of The Lewinson Brothers showed him some productions of his clients, which featured Winehouse as key vocalist. When he asked who the singer was, the manager told him he was not allowed to say. Having decided that he wanted to sign her, it took several months of asking around for Beese to eventually discover who the singer was. However, Winehouse had already recorded a number of songs and signed a publishing deal with EMI by this time. Incidentally, she formed a working relationship with producer <a href="/wiki/Salaam_Remi" title="Salaam Remi">Salaam Remi</a> through these record publishers.<sup id="cite_ref-HQ_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HQ-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Beese introduced Winehouse to his boss, Nick Gatfield, and the Island head shared his enthusiasm in signing the young artist. Winehouse was signed to Island, as rival interest in Winehouse had started to build to include representatives of EMI and Virgin starting to make moves. Beese told <i><a href="/wiki/HitQuarters" title="HitQuarters">HitQuarters</a></i> that he felt the excitement over an artist who was an atypical pop star for the time was due to a backlash against reality TV music shows, which included audiences starved for fresh, genuine young talent.<sup id="cite_ref-HQ_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HQ-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2003.E2.80.932005:_Debut_album_Frank"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2003\xe2\x80\x932005:_Debut_album_Frank">2003\xe2\x80\x932005: Debut album <i>Frank</i></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Amy_Winehouse_2004.jpg/170px-Amy_Winehouse_2004.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Amy_Winehouse_2004.jpg/255px-Amy_Winehouse_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Amy_Winehouse_2004.jpg/340px-Amy_Winehouse_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="709" data-file-height="1063" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_2004.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winehouse performing live in July 2004</div></div></div>\n<p>Winehouse\'s debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Frank_(Amy_Winehouse_album)" title="Frank (Amy Winehouse album)">Frank</a></i>, was released on 20 October 2003. Produced mainly by Salaam Remi, many songs were influenced by jazz and, apart from two <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">covers</a>, Winehouse co-wrote every song. The album received positive reviews<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> with compliments over the "cool, critical gaze" in its lyrics<sup id="cite_ref-Frank_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frank-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and brought comparisons of her voice to <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Vaughan" title="Sarah Vaughan">Sarah Vaughan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Macy_Gray" title="Macy Gray">Macy Gray</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-Frank_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frank-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The album entered the upper levels of the UK album chart in 2004 when it was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a> in the categories of "British Female Solo Artist" and "British Urban Act." It went on to achieve <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Music recording sales certification">platinum</a> sales.<sup id="cite_ref-AW_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201255_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201255-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Later in 2004, she and Remi won the <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Awards" title="Ivor Novello Awards">Ivor Novello Award</a> for Best Contemporary Song, for their first single together, "<a href="/wiki/Stronger_Than_Me" title="Stronger Than Me">Stronger Than Me</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The album was also shortlisted for the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Prize" title="Mercury Prize">2004 Mercury Music Prize</a>. In the same year, she performed at the <a href="/wiki/2004_Glastonbury_Festival_%E2%80%93_Jazzworld" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Glastonbury Festival \xe2\x80\x93 Jazzworld">Glastonbury Festival \xe2\x80\x93 Jazzworld</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2004_V_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 V Festival">V Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_International_Jazz_Festival" title="Montreal International Jazz Festival">Montreal International Jazz Festival</a> (7 July 2004, at the Club Soda). After the release of the album, Winehouse commented that she was "only 80 percent behind [the] album" because Island Records had over-ruled her preferences for the songs and mixes to be included.<sup id="cite_ref-C&amp;D_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C&amp;D-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Further singles from the album were "<a href="/wiki/Take_the_Box" title="Take the Box">Take the Box</a>," "<a href="/wiki/In_My_Bed_(Amy_Winehouse_song)" title="In My Bed (Amy Winehouse song)">In My Bed</a>"/"<a href="/wiki/You_Sent_Me_Flying" title="You Sent Me Flying">You Sent Me Flying</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Fuck_Me_Pumps" title="Fuck Me Pumps">Pumps</a>"/"<a href="/wiki/Help_Yourself_(Amy_Winehouse_song)" title="Help Yourself (Amy Winehouse song)">Help Yourself</a>."\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2006.E2.80.932007:_international_success.2C_Back_to_Black_and_touring"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2006\xe2\x80\x932007:_international_success,_Back_to_Black_and_touring">2006\xe2\x80\x932007: international success, <i>Back to Black</i> and touring</span></h3>\n<p>In contrast to her jazz-influenced former album, Winehouse\'s focus shifted to the <a href="/wiki/Girl_group" title="Girl group">girl groups</a> of the 1950s and 1960s. Winehouse hired New York singer <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Jones_(singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharon Jones (singer)">Sharon Jones</a>\'s longtime band, the <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Jones_%26_The_Dap-Kings" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharon Jones &amp; The Dap-Kings">Dap-Kings</a>, to back her up in the studio and on tour.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Mitch Winehouse relates in <i>Amy, My Daughter</i> how fascinating watching her process was: her perfectionism in the studio and how she would put what she had sung on a CD and play it in his taxi outside to know how most people would hear her music.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201271_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201271-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In May 2006, Winehouse\'s demo tracks such as "<a href="/wiki/You_Know_I%27m_No_Good" title="You Know I&#39;m No Good">You Know I\'m No Good</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Rehab_(Amy_Winehouse_song)" title="Rehab (Amy Winehouse song)">Rehab</a>" appeared on <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ronson" title="Mark Ronson">Mark Ronson</a>\'s New York radio show on <a href="/wiki/East_Village_Radio" title="East Village Radio">East Village Radio</a>. These were some of the first new songs played on the radio after the release of "Pumps" and both were slated to appear on her second album. The 11-track album, completed in five months,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201271_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201271-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> was produced entirely by Salaam Remi and Ronson, with the production credits being split between them. Ronson said in a 2010 interview that he liked working with Winehouse because she was blunt when she did not like his work.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> She in turn thought that when they first met, he was a sound engineer and that she was expecting an older man with a beard.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201268_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201268-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Promotion of <i>Back to Black</i> soon began and, in early October 2006 Winehouse\'s official website was relaunched with a new layout and clips of previously unreleased songs.<sup id="cite_ref-AW_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AW-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_Black" title="Back to Black">Back to Black</a></i> was released in the UK on 30 October 2006. It went to number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> for two weeks in January 2007, dropping then climbing back for several weeks in February. In the US, it entered at number seven on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>. It was the best-selling album in the UK of 2007, selling 1.85<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million copies over the course of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_in_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Amy_Winehouse_in_2007.jpg/170px-Amy_Winehouse_in_2007.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Amy_Winehouse_in_2007.jpg/255px-Amy_Winehouse_in_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Amy_Winehouse_in_2007.jpg/340px-Amy_Winehouse_in_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_in_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winehouse at the Avalon in Boston, Massachusetts, 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>The album spawned a number of hit singles. The first single released from the album was the Ronson-produced "Rehab." The song reached the top ten in the UK and the US.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> <i>Time</i> magazine named "Rehab" the Best Song of 2007. Writer Josh Tyrangiel praised Winehouse for her confidence, saying, "What she is mouthy, funny, sultry, and quite possibly crazy" and "It\'s impossible not to be seduced by her originality. Combine it with production by Mark Ronson that references four decades worth of soul music without once ripping it off, and you\'ve got the best song of 2007."<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The album\'s second single and lead single in the US, "You Know I\'m No Good," was released in January 2007 with a <a href="/wiki/Remix" title="Remix">remix</a> featuring rap vocals by <a href="/wiki/Ghostface_Killah" title="Ghostface Killah">Ghostface Killah</a>. It ultimately reached number 18 on the UK singles chart. The title track, "<a href="/wiki/Back_to_Black_(song)" title="Back to Black (song)">Back to Black</a>," was released in the UK in April 2007 and peaked at number 25, but was more successful across <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">mainland Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Tears_Dry_on_Their_Own" title="Tears Dry on Their Own">Tears Dry on Their Own</a>," "<a href="/wiki/Love_Is_a_Losing_Game" title="Love Is a Losing Game">Love Is a Losing Game</a>" were also released as singles, but failed to achieve the same level of success.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A deluxe edition of <i>Back to Black</i> was also released on 5 November 2007 in the UK. The bonus disc features <a href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side" title="A-side and B-side">B-sides</a>, rare, and live tracks, as well as "Valerie." Winehouse\'s debut DVD <i><a href="/wiki/I_Told_You_I_Was_Trouble:_Live_in_London" title="I Told You I Was Trouble: Live in London">I Told You I Was Trouble: Live in London</a></i> was released the same day in the UK and 13 November in the US. It includes a live set recorded at London\'s <a href="/wiki/Shepherd%27s_Bush_Empire" title="Shepherd&#39;s Bush Empire">Shepherd\'s Bush Empire</a> and a 50-minute documentary charting the singer\'s career over the previous four years.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Frank_(Amy_Winehouse_album)" title="Frank (Amy Winehouse album)">Frank</a></i> was released in the United States on 20 November 2007 to positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at number 61 on the Billboard 200 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> In addition to her own album, she collaborated with other artists on singles. Winehouse was a vocalist on the song "<a href="/wiki/Valerie_(Amy_Winehouse_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Valerie (Amy Winehouse song)">Valerie</a>" on Ronson\'s solo album <i><a href="/wiki/Version_(album)" title="Version (album)">Version</a></i>. The song peaked at number two in the UK, upon its October single release. "Valerie" was nominated for a 2008 <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Award</a> for "Best British Single."<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Her work with ex-<a href="/wiki/Sugababes" title="Sugababes">Sugababe</a> <a href="/wiki/Mutya_Buena" title="Mutya Buena">Mutya Buena</a>, "<a href="/wiki/B_Boy_Baby" title="B Boy Baby">B Boy Baby</a>," was released on 17 December 2007. It served as the fourth single from Buena\'s debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Real_Girl" title="Real Girl">Real Girl</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse was also in talks of working with <a href="/wiki/Missy_Elliott" title="Missy Elliott">Missy Elliott</a> for her album, <i><a href="/wiki/Block_Party_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Block Party (album)">Block Party</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Rolling_Stones_with_Amy_Winehouse_at_the_Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/The_Rolling_Stones_with_Amy_Winehouse_at_the_Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007.JPG/220px-The_Rolling_Stones_with_Amy_Winehouse_at_the_Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/The_Rolling_Stones_with_Amy_Winehouse_at_the_Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007.JPG/330px-The_Rolling_Stones_with_Amy_Winehouse_at_the_Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/The_Rolling_Stones_with_Amy_Winehouse_at_the_Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007.JPG/440px-The_Rolling_Stones_with_Amy_Winehouse_at_the_Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Rolling_Stones_with_Amy_Winehouse_at_the_Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winehouse with <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> at the 2007 Isle of Wight Festival</div></div></div>\n<p>Winehouse toured in conjunction with the <i>Back to Black</i> album\'s release, performing headliners in September and November 2006, including a <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Noise_Sessions" title="Little Noise Sessions">Little Noise Sessions</a></i> charity concert at the <a href="/wiki/Union_Chapel,_Islington" title="Union Chapel, Islington">Union Chapel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Islington" title="Islington">Islington</a>, North London. On 31 December 2006, Winehouse appeared on <a href="/wiki/Jools_Holland" title="Jools Holland">Jools Holland</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Hootenanny_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hootenanny (UK TV series)">Annual Hootenanny</a> live on the BBC and performed a cover of <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Gaye" title="Marvin Gaye">Marvin Gaye</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/I_Heard_It_Through_the_Grapevine" title="I Heard It Through the Grapevine">I Heard It Through the Grapevine</a>" along with <a href="/wiki/Paul_Weller" title="Paul Weller">Paul Weller</a> and Holland\'s Rhythm and Blues Orchestra. She also performed <a href="/wiki/Toots_and_the_Maytals" title="Toots and the Maytals">Toots and the Maytals</a>\' "Monkey Man". She began a run of another fourteen gigs beginning in February 2007. At his request, Hollywood star <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Willis" title="Bruce Willis">Bruce Willis</a> introduced Winehouse before her performance of "Rehab" at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2007 MTV Movie Awards">2007 MTV Movie Awards</a> in Universal City, California. She had made awards organizers nervous when she went on a <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> jaunt in the hours before the show.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> During the summer of 2007, she performed at various festivals, including the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight_Festival_2007" title="Isle of Wight Festival 2007">Isle of Wight Festival</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a> in England, <a href="/wiki/Lollapalooza" title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a> festival in Chicago, Belgium\'s <a href="/wiki/Rock_Werchter" title="Rock Werchter">Rock Werchter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Festival" title="Virgin Festival">Virgin Music Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The rest of her tour, however, did not go as well. In November 2007 the opening night of a 17-date tour was marred by booing and walkouts at the <a href="/wiki/National_Indoor_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="National Indoor Arena">National Indoor Arena</a> in Birmingham. A critic for the <i><a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Mail" title="Birmingham Mail">Birmingham Mail</a></i> said it was "one of the saddest nights of my life...I saw a supremely talented artist reduced to tears, stumbling around the stage and, unforgivably, swearing at the audience."<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Other concerts ended similarly, with, for example, fans at her <a href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Apollo" title="Hammersmith Apollo">Hammersmith Apollo</a> performance in London saying that she "looked highly intoxicated throughout,"<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> until she announced on 27 November 2007, that her performances and public appearances were cancelled for the remainder of the year, citing her doctor\'s advice to take a complete rest. A statement issued by concert promoter <a href="/wiki/Live_Nation_Entertainment" title="Live Nation Entertainment">Live Nation</a> blamed "the rigours involved in touring and the intense emotional strain that Amy has been under in recent weeks" for the decision.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Mitch Winehouse wrote about her nervousness before public performances in his 2012 book, <i>Amy, My Daughter.</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008:_Continued_success_and_acclaim">2008: Continued success and acclaim</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_-Virgin_Festival,_Pimlico,_Baltimore,_Maryland-4August2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Amy_Winehouse_-Virgin_Festival%2C_Pimlico%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland-4August2007.jpg/170px-Amy_Winehouse_-Virgin_Festival%2C_Pimlico%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland-4August2007.jpg" width="170" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Amy_Winehouse_-Virgin_Festival%2C_Pimlico%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland-4August2007.jpg/255px-Amy_Winehouse_-Virgin_Festival%2C_Pimlico%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland-4August2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Amy_Winehouse_-Virgin_Festival%2C_Pimlico%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland-4August2007.jpg/340px-Amy_Winehouse_-Virgin_Festival%2C_Pimlico%2C_Baltimore%2C_Maryland-4August2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1794" data-file-height="2945" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_-Virgin_Festival,_Pimlico,_Baltimore,_Maryland-4August2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winehouse performing at the Virgin Festival, Pimlico, Baltimore in 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>On 13 January 2008, <i>Back to Black</i> held the number-one position on the <i>Billboard</i> Pan European charts for the third consecutive week.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> On 20 February 2008, Winehouse performed at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Brit_Awards" title="2008 Brit Awards">2008 Brit Awards</a>, performing "Valerie" with Mark Ronson, followed by "Love Is a Losing Game." She urged the crowd to "make some noise for my Blake."<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2008, Winehouse also won <a href="/wiki/50th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="50th Annual Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> in the following categories: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Song of the Year">Song of the Year</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a> for the single "Rehab," and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album">Best Pop Vocal Album</a>. Additionally, <i>Back to Black</i> was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Ronson\'s work with her won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Producer_of_the_Year,_Non-Classical" title="Grammy Award for Producer of the Year, Non-Classical">Grammy Award for Producer of the Year, in the non-classical</a> category.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The singer also earned a Grammy as <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_New_Artist" title="Grammy Award for Best New Artist">Best New Artist</a>, earning her an entry in the 2009 edition of the <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness Book of World Records</a> for Most Grammy Awards won by a British Female Act.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> She ended her acceptance speech for Record of the Year with, "This is for London because Camden town ain\'t burning down," in reference to the <a href="/wiki/Camden_Market" title="Camden Market">Camden Market</a> fire.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse was forced to perform "You Know I\'m No Good" and "Rehab" for the awards ceremony via satellite, as her visa approval had not been processed in time.<sup id="cite_ref-Mitch_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mitch-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the Grammys, the album\'s sales increased, catapulting <i>Back to Black</i> to number two on the US <i>Billboard</i> 200, after it initially peaked in the seventh position.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> A special deluxe edition of <i>Back to Black</i> topped the UK album charts on 2 March 2008. Meanwhile, the original edition of the album was ranked at number 30 in its 68th week on the charts, while <i>Frank</i> charted at number 35.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Paris, she performed what was described as a "well-executed 40-minute" set at the opening of a <a href="/wiki/Fendi" title="Fendi">Fendi</a> boutique in early March.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> By 12 March, the album had sold a total of 2,467,575 copies\xe2\x80\x94318,350 copies had been sold in the previous 10 weeks\xe2\x80\x94putting the album on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_of_the_2000s_(decade)_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of best-selling albums of the 2000s (decade) in the United Kingdom">UK\'s top-10 best-selling albums of the 21st century</a> for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On 7 April, <i>Back to Black</i> was in the top position of the pan-European charts for the sixth consecutive and thirteenth aggregate week.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <i>Amy Winehouse \xe2\x80\x93 The Girl Done Good: A Documentary Review</i>, a 78-minute DVD, was released on 14 April 2008. The documentary features interviews with those who knew her at a young age, people who helped her achieve success, jazz music experts, and music and pop-culture specialists.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Awards" title="Ivor Novello Awards">Ivor Novello Awards</a> in May, Winehouse became the first-ever artist to receive two nominations for the top award: best song, musically and lyrically. She won the award for "Love Is a Losing Game" and was nominated for "You Know I\'m No Good."<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> "Rehab," a Novello winner for best contemporary song in 2006, also received a 2008 nomination for best-selling British song.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse was also nominated for a 2008 <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Award</a> in the "Act of the Year" category.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although her father, manager and various members of her touring team reportedly tried to dissuade her, Winehouse performed at the <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio_Lisboa" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock in Rio Lisboa">Rock in Rio Lisboa</a> festival in Portugal in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Although the set was plagued by a late arrival and problems with her voice, the crowd warmed to her. In addition to her own material she performed two <a href="/wiki/The_Specials" title="The Specials">Specials</a> covers.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse performed at <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>\'s 90th Birthday Party concert at London\'s <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park</a> on 27 June,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and the next day at the Glastonbury Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> On 12 July, at the <a href="/wiki/Oxegen" title="Oxegen">Oxegen Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> she performed a well-received 50-minute set<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> which was followed the next day by a 14-song set at <a href="/wiki/T_in_the_Park" title="T in the Park">T in the Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 August she played at the <a href="/wiki/Staffordshire" title="Staffordshire">Staffordshire</a> leg of the V Festival, and the following day played the <a href="/wiki/Chelmsford" title="Chelmsford">Chelmsford</a> leg of the festival. Organizers said that Winehouse attracted the biggest crowds of the festival. Audience reaction was reported as mixed.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On 6 September, she was <a href="/wiki/Bestival_Saturday_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Bestival Saturday 2008">Bestival\'s Saturday headliner</a>, where her performance was described as polished\xe2\x80\x94terminated by a curfew as the show running overdue, after Winehouse started an hour late\xe2\x80\x94and her storming off stage.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A clip of Winehouse\'s music was included in the "Roots and Influences" area that looked at connections between different artists at the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame Annex NYC</a>, which opened in December 2008. One thread started with <a href="/wiki/Billie_Holiday" title="Billie Holiday">Billie Holiday</a>, continued with <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>, and then finished with Winehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>Back to Black</i> was the world\'s seventh-biggest-selling album of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The album\'s sales meant that the market performance of <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music_Group" title="Universal Music Group">Universal Music\'s</a> recorded music division did not drop to levels experienced by the overall music market.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2009.E2.80.932011:_Final_projects_before_death"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2009\xe2\x80\x932011:_Final_projects_before_death">2009\xe2\x80\x932011: Final projects before death</span></h3>\n<p>In a poll of US residents conducted for <a href="/wiki/VisitBritain" title="VisitBritain">VisitBritain</a> by Harris Interactive, the results of which were released in March 2009, one-fifth of those polled indicated they had listened to Winehouse\'s music during the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse performed with <a href="/wiki/Rhythms_del_Mundo" title="Rhythms del Mundo">Rhythms del Mundo</a> on their cover of the <a href="/wiki/Sam_Cooke" title="Sam Cooke">Sam Cooke</a> song, "<a href="/wiki/Cupid_(Sam_Cooke_song)" title="Cupid (Sam Cooke song)">Cupid</a>", for an <i>Artists Project Earth</i> benefit album that was released on 13 July 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse and Ronson contributed a cover of <a href="/wiki/Lesley_Gore" title="Lesley Gore">Lesley Gore</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_My_Party_(Lesley_Gore_song)" title="It&#39;s My Party (Lesley Gore song)">It\'s My Party</a>" to the <a href="/wiki/Quincy_Jones" title="Quincy Jones">Quincy Jones</a> tribute album <i><a href="/wiki/Q_Soul_Bossa_Nostra" title="Q Soul Bossa Nostra">Q Soul Bossa Nostra</a></i> released 9 November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse and drummer <a href="/wiki/Questlove" title="Questlove">Questlove</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a> had agreed to form a group but her problems obtaining a visa delayed their working together: <a href="/wiki/Salaam_Remi" title="Salaam Remi">Salaam Remi</a> had already created some material with Winehouse as part of the project.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Music">Universal Music</a> pressed her for new material in 2008, and Winehouse as of 2 September had not been near a recording studio.<sup id="cite_ref-Times_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In late October Winehouse\'s spokesman was quoted as saying that Winehouse had not been given a deadline to complete her third album, for which she was learning to play drums.<sup id="cite_ref-Nov_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nov-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_with_backing_singers_Zalon_and_Heshima_Thompson.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Amy_Winehouse_with_backing_singers_Zalon_and_Heshima_Thompson.jpg/220px-Amy_Winehouse_with_backing_singers_Zalon_and_Heshima_Thompson.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Amy_Winehouse_with_backing_singers_Zalon_and_Heshima_Thompson.jpg/330px-Amy_Winehouse_with_backing_singers_Zalon_and_Heshima_Thompson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Amy_Winehouse_with_backing_singers_Zalon_and_Heshima_Thompson.jpg/440px-Amy_Winehouse_with_backing_singers_Zalon_and_Heshima_Thompson.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_with_backing_singers_Zalon_and_Heshima_Thompson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Amy Winehouse with her band backstage, 16 March 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>In May 2009 Winehouse returned to performing at a jazz festival in Saint Lucia amid torrential downpours and technical difficulties. During her set it was reported she was unsteady on her feet and had trouble remembering lyrics. She apologised to the crowd for being "bored" and ended the set in the middle of a song.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> To a cheering crowd on 23 August at the V festival, Winehouse sang with <a href="/wiki/The_Specials" title="The Specials">The Specials</a> on their songs "You\'re Wondering Now" and "<a href="/wiki/Ghost_Town_(The_Specials_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghost Town (The Specials song)">Ghost Town</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> During her stay in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, she also worked on new music with <a href="/wiki/Salaam_Remi" title="Salaam Remi">Salaam Remi</a>. <a href="/wiki/Island_Records" title="Island Records">Island</a> claimed that a new album would be due in 2010 with Island co-president Darcus Beese saying, "I\'ve heard a couple of song demos that have absolutely floored me."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In July 2010, Winehouse was quoted as saying her next album would be released no later than January 2011, saying "It\'s going to be very much the same as my second album, where there\'s a lot of jukebox stuff and songs that are... just jukebox, really." Ronson said the same month however that he had not started to record the album.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> She performed "Valerie" with Ronson at a movie premiere but forgot some of the song\'s lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In October Winehouse performed a four-song set to promote her fashion line. In December 2010, she played a 40-minute concert at a <a href="/wiki/Russian_oligarch" title="Russian oligarch">Russian oligarch</a>\'s party in Moscow, the tycoon hand picking the songs.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During January 2011, she played five dates in Brazil, with <a href="/wiki/Opening_act" title="Opening act">opening acts</a> of <a href="/wiki/Janelle_Mon%C3%A1e" title="Janelle Mon\xc3\xa1e">Janelle Mon\xc3\xa1e</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayer_Hawthorne" title="Mayer Hawthorne">Mayer Hawthorne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> On 11 February 2011, Winehouse cut short a performance in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> following booing from the audience. Winehouse was reported to be tired, distracted and "tipsy" during the performance.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 June 2011, Winehouse started her twelve-leg 2011 European tour in <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>. Local media described her performance as a scandal and disaster, and she was booed off the stage due to her apparently being too drunk to perform. It was reported that she was unable to remember the city she was in, the lyrics of her songs or\xe2\x80\x94when trying to introduce them\xe2\x80\x94the names of the members of her band.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The local press also claimed that Winehouse was forced to perform by her bodyguards, who did not allow her to leave the stage when she tried to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> She then pulled out of performances in Istanbul and Athens which had been scheduled for the following week.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> On 21 June, it was announced that she had cancelled all shows of her tour and would be given "as long as it takes" to sort herself out.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse\'s last public appearance took place at Camden\'s <a href="/wiki/Roundhouse_(venue)" title="Roundhouse (venue)">Roundhouse</a>, London on 20 July 2011, when she made a surprise appearance on stage to support her goddaughter, <a href="/wiki/Dionne_Bromfield" title="Dionne Bromfield">Dionne Bromfield</a>, who was singing "Mama Said" with <a href="/wiki/The_Wanted" title="The Wanted">The Wanted</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse died on 23 July 2011. On the week of 26 July 2011, <i>Frank</i>, <i>Back to Black</i> and the <i>Back to Black</i> <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> re-entered the <i>Billboard</i> 200 at number 57, number 9 and number 152 respectively, with the album climbing to number 4 the following week.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> <i>Back to Black</i> also topped the <i>Billboard</i> Digital Albums chart on the same week and was the second best-seller on iTunes.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> "Rehab" re-entered and topped the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Digital_Songs" title="Digital Songs">Hot Digital Songs</a> chart as well, selling up to 38,000 more <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">digital downloads</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> As of August 2011, "Back to Black" was the best-selling album in the UK in the twenty-first century.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse\'s last recording was a duet with American singer <a href="/wiki/Tony_Bennett" title="Tony Bennett">Tony Bennett</a> for his latest album, <i><a href="/wiki/Duets_II_(Tony_Bennett_album)" title="Duets II (Tony Bennett album)">Duets II</a></i>, released on 20 September 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Their single from the album, "Body and Soul," was released on 14 September 2011 on MTV and VH1 to commemorate what would have been her 28th birthday. Her father, Mitch Winehouse, launched the Amy Winehouse Foundation with the goal of raising awareness and support for organisations that help vulnerable, young adults with problems such as addiction. Proceeds from "Body and Soul" benefit the Amy Winehouse Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The song received the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a> for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Duo/Group_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Duo/Group Performance">Best Pop Duo/Group Performance</a> at the <a href="/wiki/54th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Annual Grammy Awards">54th Grammy Awards</a> on 12 February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse\'s father picked up the award at the awards ceremony with his wife Janis, saying, "We shouldn\'t be here. Our darling daughter should be here. These are the cards that we\'re dealt."<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When interviewed by <a href="/wiki/Jon_Stewart" title="Jon Stewart">Jon Stewart</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">The Daily Show</a></i> on 29 September 2011, Bennett stated that in hindsight, he believed that Winehouse:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><dl><dd>was in trouble at that time because she had a couple of engagements that she didn\'t keep up. But what people didn\'t realise at that time, that she really knew, and in fact I didn\'t even know it when we were making the record, and now looking at the whole thing; she knew that she was in a lot of trouble; that she wasn\'t going to live. And it wasn\'t drugs. It was alcohol toward the end... It was such a sad thing because... she was the only singer that really sang what I call the \'right way\' because she was a great jazz-pop singer... She was really a great jazz singer. A true jazz singer. And I regret that because that\'s the \'right way\' to sing.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></dd></dl>\n<p>An album of previously unreleased material, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Lioness:_Hidden_Treasures" title="Lioness: Hidden Treasures">Lioness: Hidden Treasures</a></i>, was released on 6 December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at the top of the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> with the biggest first-week sales of Winehouse\'s career.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at number five on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, selling 114,000 units, making it her highest-debuting album in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Image">Image</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Ronettes.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/The_Ronettes.JPG/170px-The_Ronettes.JPG" width="170" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/The_Ronettes.JPG/255px-The_Ronettes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/The_Ronettes.JPG/340px-The_Ronettes.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1282" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Ronettes.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winehouse was influenced by soul girl groups such as <a href="/wiki/The_Ronettes" title="The Ronettes">The Ronettes</a>, whose look she imitated.</div></div></div>\n<p>Winehouse\'s greatest love was 1960s <a href="/wiki/Girl_group" title="Girl group">girl groups</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sisario_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sisario-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Her stylist, Alex Foden, borrowed her "instantly recognisable" <a href="/wiki/Beehive_(hairstyle)" title="Beehive (hairstyle)">beehive</a> hairdo (a <a href="/wiki/Artificial_hair_integrations" title="Artificial hair integrations">weave</a><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoffman_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>) and she borrowed her <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra" title="Cleopatra">Cleopatra</a> makeup from <a href="/wiki/The_Ronettes" title="The Ronettes">The Ronettes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sisario_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sisario-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Her imitation was so successful, as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> reports: "<a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Spector" title="Ronnie Spector">Ronnie Spector</a>\xe2\x80\x94who, it could be argued, all but invented Winehouse\'s style in the first place when she took the stage at the Brooklyn Fox Theater with her fellow Ronettes more than 40 years ago\xe2\x80\x94was so taken aback at a picture of Winehouse in the <i>New York Post</i> that she exclaimed, "I don\'t know her, I never met her, and when I saw that pic, I thought, \'That\'s me!\' But then I found out, no, it\'s Amy! I didn\'t have on my glasses."<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> style reporter, Guy Trebay, discussed the multiplicity of influences on Winehouse\'s style after her death. Trebay noted, "her stylish husband, Blake Fielder-Civil, may have influenced her look." Additionally, Trebay observed:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>She was a 5-foot-3 almanac of visual reference, most famously to Ronnie Spector of the Ronettes, but also to the white British soul singer <a href="/wiki/Mari_Wilson" title="Mari Wilson">Mari Wilson</a>, less famous for her sound than her beehive; to the punk god <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Thunders" title="Johnny Thunders">Johnny Thunders</a>...; to the fierce <a href="/wiki/Council_house" title="Council house">council-house</a> chicks... (see: <a href="/wiki/Dior" class="mw-redirect" title="Dior">Dior</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chanel" title="Chanel">Chanel</a> runways, 2007 and 2008) ... to a lineage of bad girls, extending from Cleopatra to <a href="/wiki/Louise_Brooks" title="Louise Brooks">Louise Brooks</a>\'s Lulu and including <a href="/wiki/Salt-n-Pepa" class="mw-redirect" title="Salt-n-Pepa">Salt-n-Pepa</a>, to irresistible man traps that always seemed to come to the same unfortunate end.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Former <i>Rolling Stone</i> editor Joe Levy, who had put her on the magazine\'s cover, broke her look down this way:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Just as her best music drew on sampling \xe2\x80\x93 assembling sonic licks and stylistic fragments borrowed from <a href="/wiki/Motown" title="Motown">Motown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stax_Records" title="Stax Records">Stax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a> and early <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip-hop</a> \xe2\x80\x93 her personal style was also a knowing <a href="/wiki/Collage" title="Collage">collage</a>. There was a certain moment in the \'90s when, if you were headed downtown and turned left, every girl looked like <a href="/wiki/Bettie_Page" title="Bettie Page">Bettie Page</a>. But they did not do what Winehouse did, mixing <a href="/wiki/Bettie_Page" title="Bettie Page">Bettie Page</a> with <a href="/wiki/Brigitte_Bardot" title="Brigitte Bardot">Brigitte Bardot</a> and adding that little bit of Ronnie Spector.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Mitch Winehouse later revealed that the influence for the bold red lipstick, thick eyebrows and heavy eyeliner came from Latinas she saw in Miami, on her trip there to work with Salaam Remi on <i>Back to Black.</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201270_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201270-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> This same look, however, was repeatedly denigrated by the British press. At the same time that the <a href="/wiki/NME_Awards" title="NME Awards">NME Awards</a> nominated Winehouse in the categories of "Best Solo Artist" and "Best Music DVD" in 2008, they awarded her "Worst Dressed Performer."<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse was also ranked number two on <a href="/wiki/Richard_Blackwell" title="Richard Blackwell">Richard Blackwell</a>\'s 48th annual "Ten Worst Dressed Women" list, behind <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Beckham" title="Victoria Beckham">Victoria Beckham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dionne_Bromfield.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dionne_Bromfield.jpg/180px-Dionne_Bromfield.jpg" width="180" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dionne_Bromfield.jpg/270px-Dionne_Bromfield.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Dionne_Bromfield.jpg/360px-Dionne_Bromfield.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="2822" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dionne_Bromfield.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first act on Winehouse\'s record label was her goddaughter <a href="/wiki/Dionne_Bromfield" title="Dionne Bromfield">Dionne Bromfield</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Winehouse joined a campaign to stop a block of flats being built beside the <a href="/wiki/George_Tavern" title="George Tavern">George Tavern</a>, a famous London <a href="/wiki/East_End" class="mw-redirect" title="East End">East End</a> music venue. Campaign supporters feared the residential development would end the spot\'s lucrative sideline as a film and photo location, on which it relies to survive.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> As part of a breast cancer awareness campaign, Winehouse appeared in a revealing photograph for the April 2008 issue of <i>Easy Living</i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse had an estimated \xc2\xa310m fortune, tying her for tenth place in the 2008 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> listing of the wealth of musicians under age 30.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The following year her fortune had dropped to an estimated \xc2\xa35m.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Her finances are run by Mitch and Janis Winehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> It was reported she earned about \xc2\xa31m singing at two private parties during <a href="/wiki/Paris_Fashion_Week" title="Paris Fashion Week">Paris Fashion Week</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> as well as another \xc2\xa31m to perform at a Moscow Art Gallery for Russian oligarch <a href="/wiki/Roman_Abramovich" title="Roman Abramovich">Roman Abramovich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse loaned a vintage dress used in her video for "Tears Dry on Their Own" as well as a DVD to the <a href="/wiki/British_Music_Experience" title="British Music Experience">British Music Experience</a>, a new museum dedicated to the history of British pop music.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The museum, located in <a href="/wiki/The_O2" title="The O2">The O2</a>, opened on 9 March 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2009, Winehouse announced that she was launching her own record label. The first act on her <a href="/wiki/Lioness_Records" title="Lioness Records">Lioness Records</a> is Winehouse\'s 13-year-old goddaughter, <a href="/wiki/Dionne_Bromfield" title="Dionne Bromfield">Dionne Bromfield</a>. Her first album, featuring covers of classic soul records, was released on 12 October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse is the backing singer on several tracks on the album and she performed backing vocals for Bromfield on the television programme <i><a href="/wiki/Strictly_Come_Dancing" title="Strictly Come Dancing">Strictly Come Dancing</a></i> on 10 October.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse and her family are the subject of a 2009 documentary shot by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Daphne_Barak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Daphne Barak (page does not exist)">Daphne Barak</a> titled <i>Saving Amy</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse entered into a joint venture in 2009 with <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> to launch a range of wrapping paper and gift cards containing song lyrics from her album <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_Black" title="Back to Black">Back to Black</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> On 8 January 2010, a television documentary, <i>My Daughter Amy</i>, aired on <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">Channel 4</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> <i>Saving Amy</i> was released as a paperback book in January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse collaborated on a 17 piece fashion collection with the Fred Perry label. It was released for sale in October 2010. According to Fred Perry\'s marketing director "We had three major design meetings where she was closely involved in product style selection and the application of fabric, colour and styling details," and gave "crucial input on proportion, colour and fit." The collection consists of "vintage-inspired looks including <a href="/wiki/Capri_pants" title="Capri pants">Capri pants</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Bowling" title="Bowling">bowling</a> dress, a <a href="/wiki/Trench_coat" title="Trench coat">trench coat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pencil_skirt" title="Pencil skirt">pencil skirts</a>, a longline <a href="/wiki/Argyle_(pattern)" title="Argyle (pattern)">argyle</a> sweater and a pink-and-black checkerboard-printed collared shirt."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> At the behest of her family, three forthcoming collections up to and including autumn/winter 2012 that she had designed prior to her death will be released.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WinehouseLA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Knee high portrait of woman in her twenties wearing a short gathered skirt, light grey dress and dark cardigan" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/WinehouseLA.jpg/170px-WinehouseLA.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/WinehouseLA.jpg/255px-WinehouseLA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7b/WinehouseLA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="333" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WinehouseLA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Winehouse in Los Angeles, 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>Winehouse\'s <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dichotomous" class="extiw" title="wikt:dichotomous">dichotomous</a> public image of critical and commercial success versus personal turmoil prompted media comment. The <i><a href="/wiki/New_Statesman" title="New Statesman">New Statesman</a></i> called Winehouse "a filthy-mouthed, down-to-earth <a href="/wiki/Diva" title="Diva">diva</a>,"<sup id="cite_ref-NS_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NS-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> called her "a perfect storm of sex kitten, raw talent and poor impulse control."<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Karen Heller with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Philadelphia_Inquirer" title="The Philadelphia Inquirer">The Philadelphia Inquirer</a></i> summarised the maelstrom this way:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>She\'s only 24 with six Grammy nominations, crashing headfirst into success and despair, with a codependent husband in jail, exhibitionist parents with questionable judgement, and the <a href="/wiki/Paparazzi" title="Paparazzi">paparazzi</a> documenting her emotional and physical distress. Meanwhile, a haute designer <a href="/wiki/Karl_Lagerfeld" title="Karl Lagerfeld">Karl Lagerfeld</a> appropriates her dishevelled style and eating issues to market to the elite while proclaiming her the new <a href="/wiki/Brigitte_Bardot" title="Brigitte Bardot">Bardot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>By 2008, her continued drug problems threatened her career. As Nick Gatfield, the president of <a href="/wiki/Island_Records" title="Island Records">Island Records</a>, toyed with the idea of releasing Winehouse "to deal with her problems," he said, "It\'s a reflection of her status [in the U.S.] that when you flick through the TV coverage [of the Grammys] it\'s her image they use."<sup id="cite_ref-jan24_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jan24-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Post-Grammys, some questioned whether Winehouse should have been honoured with the awards given her recent personal and drug problems,<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Cole" title="Natalie Cole">Natalie Cole</a>, who introduced Winehouse at the ceremony and who herself battled substance-abuse problems while winning a Grammy for Best New Artist in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> (Winehouse was prevented from travelling to and performing at the Grammy Awards ceremony in the US due to failing a drug test.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>) In a newspaper commentary, the executive director of the UN Office on Drugs and Crime, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Maria_Costa" title="Antonio Maria Costa">Antonio Maria Costa</a>, said that the alleged drug habits of Winehouse and other celebrities sent a bad message "to others who are vulnerable to addiction" and undermine the efforts of other celebrities trying to raise awareness of problems in Africa, now that more cocaine used in Europe passes through that continent.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse\'s spokesperson noted that "Amy has never given a quote about drugs or flaunted it in any way. She\'s had some problems and is trying to get better.
