The U.N. should get its own house in order."<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2008, her record label stated it believed the extensive media coverage she had received increased record sales.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In an April 2008 poll conducted by <a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a>, Winehouse was named the second greatest "ultimate heroine" by the UK population at large, topping the voting for that category of those polled under 25 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-heroine_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heroine-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Psychologist Donna Dawson commented that the results demonstrated that women like Winehouse who had "a certain sense of vulnerability or have had to fight against some adversity in their lives" received recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-heroine_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heroine-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2008, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Scotland" title="BBC Radio Scotland">BBC Radio Scotland</a>\'s head, Jeff Zycinski, stated that the BBC, and media in general, were complicit in undermining celebrities, including Winehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-Broadcast_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Broadcast-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> He said that public interest in the singer\'s lifestyle did not make her lifestyle newsworthy. Rod McKenzie, editor of the BBC Radio One programme <i><a href="/wiki/Newsbeat" title="Newsbeat">Newsbeat</a></i>, replied: "If you play [Amy Winehouse\'s] music to a certain demographic, those same people want to know what\'s happening in her private life. If you don\'t cover it, you\'re insulting young licence fee payers."<sup id="cite_ref-Broadcast_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Broadcast-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Scotsman" title="The Scotsman">The Scotsman</a></i>, British singer and songwriter <a href="/wiki/Lily_Allen" title="Lily Allen">Lily Allen</a> was quoted to have said \xe2\x80\x93 "I know Amy Winehouse very well. And she is very different to what people portray her as being. Yes, she does get out of her mind on drugs sometimes, but she is also a very clever, intelligent, witty, funny person who can hold it together. You just don\'t see that side."<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Amy_Winehouse" title="List of awards and nominations received by Amy Winehouse">List of awards and nominations received by Amy Winehouse</a></div>\n<p>Among the awards and recognition for her debut album <i>Frank</i>, Winehouse earned an <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Awards" title="Ivor Novello Awards">Ivor Novello Award</a> from the British Academy of Songwriters for Best Contemporary Song ("<a href="/wiki/Stronger_Than_Me" title="Stronger Than Me">Stronger Than Me</a>"),<sup id="cite_ref-Profile_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Award</a> nomination for Best British Female Solo Artist,<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> and an inclusion in Robert Dimery\'s 2006 book, <i><a href="/wiki/1001_Albums_You_Must_Hear_Before_You_Die" title="1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die">1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Her second studio album, <i>Back to Black</i>, produced numerous nominations, including two Brit Awards (Best British Album, and won her Best British Female Solo Artist), six <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> (including five wins),<sup id="cite_ref-Grammy_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grammy-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> four Ivor Novello Awards, four <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Music Awards</a>, three <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award" title="MTV Video Music Award">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, three <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a>, and it was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Prize" title="Mercury Prize">Mercury Prize</a> (Album of the Year) and a <a href="/wiki/MOBO_Awards" title="MOBO Awards">MOBO Awards</a> (Best UK Female). During her career, Winehouse received 23 awards from 60 nominations.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reputation">Critical reputation</span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>\'s Garry Mulholland called Winehouse "the pre-eminent vocal talent of her generation".<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a>\'s Cyril Cordor, she was one of the UK\'s premier singers during the 2000s; "fans and critics alike embraced her rugged charm, brash sense of humor, and distinctively soulful and jazzy vocals".<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, Caroline Sullivan later wrote that "her idolisation of Dinah Washington and the Ronettes distinguished her from almost all newly minted pop singers of the early 2000s; her exceptionally-susceptible-to-heartbreak voice did the rest".<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> By contrast, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> dismissed Winehouse as "a self-aggrandizing self-abuser who\'s taken seriously because she makes a show of soul".<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 February 2012, Winehouse was ranked 26<sup>th</sup> on <a href="/wiki/The_Greatest_(TV_series)" title="The Greatest (TV series)">VH1\'s <i>100 Greatest Women in Music</i></a> list.<sup id="cite_ref-VH1_100_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VH1_100-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> In March 2017, singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a> said he was enjoying listening to Winehouse\'s last record (<i>Back to Black</i>), and called her "the last real individualist around."<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_work">Charity work</span></h2>\n<p>Throughout her life Winehouse donated her money, music and time to many charities, particularly those concerned with children. She was once named "the most charitable act" by <i><a href="/wiki/Popworld" title="Popworld">Pop World</a></i>. While this side of her personality was never well known to the general public, throughout both the arts community and the charity community she was known for her generosity.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Among the charities she supported are <a href="/wiki/Adopt-A-Minefield" title="Adopt-A-Minefield">Adopt-A-Minefield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anti-Slavery_International" title="Anti-Slavery International">Anti-Slavery International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breast_Cancer_Campaign" title="Breast Cancer Campaign">Breast Cancer Campaign</a>, <a href="/wiki/CARE_(relief_agency)" title="CARE (relief agency)">CARE</a>, Children of the Andes, <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Medical_Research_Institute" title="Children&#39;s Medical Research Institute">Children\'s Medical Research Institute</a>, <a href="/wiki/ChildFund" title="ChildFund">Christian Children\'s Fund</a>, City at Peace, UK charity telethon <a href="/wiki/Comic_Relief" title="Comic Relief">Comic Relief</a>, London\'s <a href="/wiki/Great_Ormond_Street_Hospital" title="Great Ormond Street Hospital">Great Ormond Street Hospital</a> for sick children, <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a>, Healthlink Worldwide, Hear the World, <a href="/wiki/Heifer_International" title="Heifer International">Heifer International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holy_Apostles_Soup_Kitchen" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Apostles Soup Kitchen">Holy Apostles Soup Kitchen</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Cross</a>, LIFEbeat, Lifeline and Rape Crisis PMB, <a href="/wiki/Opportunity_International" title="Opportunity International">Opportunity International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rights_and_Humanity" title="Rights and Humanity">Rights and Humanity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a>, <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Music_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Save the Music Foundation">Save the Music Foundation</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Jude_Children%27s_Research_Hospital" title="St. Jude Children&#39;s Research Hospital">St. Jude Children\'s Research Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teenage_Cancer_Trust" title="Teenage Cancer Trust">Teenage Cancer Trust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christina_Noble_Children%27s_Foundation" title="Christina Noble Children&#39;s Foundation">Christina Noble Children\'s Foundation</a>, Little Dreams Foundation, Lotus Outreach, <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_Children%27s_Fund" title="Nelson Mandela Children&#39;s Fund">Nelson Mandela Children\'s Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UNHCR</a>, <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, <a href="/wiki/V-Day_(movement)" title="V-Day (movement)">V-Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/WaterAid" title="WaterAid">WaterAid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/World_Neighbors" title="World Neighbors">World Neighbors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, Winehouse appeared naked in an issue of <i>Easy Living Magazine</i> to raise awareness of breast cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, she appeared on a CD called <i>Classics</i> alongside musicians such as <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Killers" title="The Killers">The Killers</a> and many Cuban musicians to raise awareness of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>. In March 2011, Winehouse donated over \xc2\xa320,000 worth of clothes to a local charity shop in London.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, it was revealed that she had paid for the medical tests for a man called Julian Jean DeBaptiste in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> in 2009. "I had surgery on 1 July 2009... it cost a fortune and Amy paid for the whole thing. I tried to thank her but she just hugged me and told me not to say anything. Her generosity gave me my life back."<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artwork_and_Tussauds_wax_figure">Artwork and Tussauds wax figure</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_wax_figure_at_Madame_Tussauds_in_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Amy_Winehouse_wax_figure_at_Madame_Tussauds_in_London.jpg/170px-Amy_Winehouse_wax_figure_at_Madame_Tussauds_in_London.jpg" width="170" height="335" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Amy_Winehouse_wax_figure_at_Madame_Tussauds_in_London.jpg/255px-Amy_Winehouse_wax_figure_at_Madame_Tussauds_in_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Amy_Winehouse_wax_figure_at_Madame_Tussauds_in_London.jpg/340px-Amy_Winehouse_wax_figure_at_Madame_Tussauds_in_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1228" data-file-height="2417" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_wax_figure_at_Madame_Tussauds_in_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wax figure of Winehouse at <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> in London</div></div></div>\n<p>London\'s <a href="/wiki/Mall_Galleries" class="mw-redirect" title="Mall Galleries">Mall Galleries</a> opened an exhibition in May 2008 that included a sculpture of Winehouse, titled <i>Excess</i>. The piece, created by Guy Portelli, had a miniature of the singer <a href="/wiki/Lying_(position)" title="Lying (position)">lying</a> on top of a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cracked" class="extiw" title="wikt:cracked">cracked</a> champagne bottle, with a pool of spilled liquid underneath. The body was covered with what appeared to be tiny pills, while one outstretched hand held a glass.<sup id="cite_ref-Sculpture_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sculpture-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Another piece, a print titled <i>Celebrity 1</i> by artist Charlotte Suckling, was shown in the same exhibition.<sup id="cite_ref-Sculpture_191-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sculpture-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A wax sculpture of Winehouse went on display at the London <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> on 23 July 2008. The singer did not attend the unveiling, although her parents did.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> A sculpture by Marco Perego, titled <i>The Only Good Rock Star Is a Dead Rock Star</i>, that depicts Winehouse lying in a pool of blood with an apple and a bullet hole in her head after being shot by American novelist and <a href="/wiki/Beat_Generation" title="Beat Generation">Beat</a> poet <a href="/wiki/William_S._Burroughs" title="William S. Burroughs">William S. Burroughs</a> (in a recreation of the accidental killing of his wife <a href="/wiki/Joan_Vollmer" title="Joan Vollmer">Joan Vollmer</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-TimesArt_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimesArt-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> was scheduled to go on display in New York\'s Half Gallery on 14 November 2008 with a sale price of US$100,000. Perego said of the sculpture: "Rock stars are the sacrificial animals of society." Winehouse\'s spokesperson stated: "It\'s a funny kind of tribute. The artist seems in thrall to a tabloid persona that is not the real Amy. People often use her image to sell their work."<sup id="cite_ref-TimesArt_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimesArt-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_Statue,_Camden_(14946739033).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Amy_Winehouse_Statue%2C_Camden_%2814946739033%29.jpg/180px-Amy_Winehouse_Statue%2C_Camden_%2814946739033%29.jpg" width="180" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Amy_Winehouse_Statue%2C_Camden_%2814946739033%29.jpg/270px-Amy_Winehouse_Statue%2C_Camden_%2814946739033%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Amy_Winehouse_Statue%2C_Camden_%2814946739033%29.jpg/360px-Amy_Winehouse_Statue%2C_Camden_%2814946739033%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="4608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_Statue,_Camden_(14946739033).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bronze statue of Winehouse in <a href="/wiki/Camden_Town" title="Camden Town">Camden Town</a>, London unveiled in September 2014</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2012, Winehouse was among the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British cultural icons</a> selected by artist Sir <a href="/wiki/Peter_Blake_(artist)" title="Peter Blake (artist)">Peter Blake</a> to appear in a new version of his most famous artwork \xe2\x80\x93 the Beatles\' <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper&#39;s Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper\'s Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> album cover \xe2\x80\x93 to celebrate the British cultural figures of his life that he most admires.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 14 September 2014 (which would have been Winehouse\'s 31st birthday), <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Amy_Winehouse" title="Statue of Amy Winehouse">a statue was unveiled of her</a>, which was created by sculptor Scott Eaton, at <a href="/wiki/Stables_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Stables Market">Stables Market</a> in <a href="/wiki/Camden_Town" title="Camden Town">Camden Town</a>, north London. Fans and relatives gathered for the unveiling in Camden\'s Stable Market, where it will be a permanent memorial to her.<sup id="cite_ref-statue_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statue-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> London-based Eaton, who sculpted the piece after being introduced to Winehouse\'s father Mitch, said the statue was meant to capture her "attitude and strength, but also give subtle hints of insecurity."<sup id="cite_ref-statue_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statue-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Her father Mitch said of the statue: "Now Amy will oversee the comings and goings of her home town forever... Amy was in love with Camden and it is the place her fans from all over the world associate her with."<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_next_generation">The next generation</span></h3>\n<p>British singer <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a> has credited Winehouse\'s success in making her and fellow British singer <a href="/wiki/Duffy_(singer)" title="Duffy (singer)">Duffy\'s</a> journey to the United States "a bit smoother."<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> credited Winehouse with paving the way for her rise to the top of the charts, explaining that Winehouse made it easier for unconventional women to have mainstream pop success.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Raphael_Saadiq" title="Raphael Saadiq">Raphael Saadiq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Hamilton_(musician)" title="Anthony Hamilton (musician)">Anthony Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a> said "Amy Winehouse was produced by people who wanted to create a marketing coup. The positive side is that it reacquainted an audience with this music and played an introductory role for others. This reinvigorated the genre by overcoming the vintage aspect."<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other artists that have credited Winehouse as an influence and/or for paving the way for them include <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Mars" title="Bruno Mars">Bruno Mars</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tove_Lo" title="Tove Lo">Tove Lo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ellie_Goulding" title="Ellie Goulding">Ellie Goulding</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jessie_J" title="Jessie J">Jessie J</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emeli_Sand%C3%A9" title="Emeli Sand\xc3\xa9">Emeli Sand\xc3\xa9</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Justice" title="Victoria Justice">Victoria Justice</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paloma_Faith" title="Paloma Faith">Paloma Faith</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lana_Del_Rey" title="Lana Del Rey">Lana Del Rey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sam_Smith_(singer)" title="Sam Smith (singer)">Sam Smith</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Florence_Welch" title="Florence Welch">Florence Welch</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Halsey_(singer)" title="Halsey (singer)">Halsey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alessia_Cara" title="Alessia Cara">Alessia Cara</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daya_(singer)" title="Daya (singer)">Daya</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Estelle_(musician)" title="Estelle (musician)">Estelle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_Black" title="Back to Black">Back to Black</a>,</i> record companies sought out female artists with a similar sound and fearless and experimental female musicians in general. Adele and Duffy were the second wave of artists with a sound similar to Winehouse\'s. A third wave of female musicians that has emerged since the album was released are led by <a href="/wiki/V_V_Brown" title="V V Brown">V V Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence_and_the_Machine" title="Florence and the Machine">Florence and the Machine</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Roux" title="La Roux">La Roux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Boots" title="Little Boots">Little Boots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> In March 2011, the <i>New York Daily News</i> ran an article attributing the continuing wave of British female artists that have been successful in the United States to Winehouse and her absence. <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> magazine music editor Charles Aaron was quoted as saying "Amy Winehouse was the <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a> moment for all these women," "They can all be traced back to her in terms of attitude, musical styles or fashion." According to Keith Caulfield, chart manager for <i>Billboard</i>, "Because of Amy, or the lack thereof, the marketplace was able to get singers like Adele, Estelle and Duffy," "Now those ladies have brought on the new ones, like <a href="/wiki/Eliza_Doolittle_(singer)" title="Eliza Doolittle (singer)">Eliza Doolittle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rumer_(musician)" title="Rumer (musician)">Rumer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ellie_Goulding" title="Ellie Goulding">Ellie</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Amy_Winehouse_Foundation">Amy Winehouse Foundation</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse_Foundation" title="Amy Winehouse Foundation">Amy Winehouse Foundation</a></div>\n<p>After the singer\'s death by alcohol intoxication in July 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse_Foundation" title="Amy Winehouse Foundation">Amy Winehouse Foundation</a> was set up by Winehouse\'s family and launched on 14 September 2011 (which would have been Winehouse\'s 28th birthday). Its aim is to help young people and it works with other charitable organisations to provide frontline support. Its central office is in North London, but it also has an office in New York (operating under the name \'The Amy Winehouse Foundation US\').<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Jon_Snow_(journalist)" title="Jon Snow (journalist)">Jon Snow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Windsor" title="Barbara Windsor">Barbara Windsor</a> are patrons for the charity, and ambassadors include <a href="/wiki/Keira_Chaplin" class="mw-redirect" title="Keira Chaplin">Keira Chaplin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mica_Paris" title="Mica Paris">Mica Paris</a>. In October 2015 <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ronson" title="Mark Ronson">Mark Ronson</a> became a patron.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Amy\'s brother Alex works full-time for the foundation, having given up his career as an online music journalist.<sup id="cite_ref-Alex_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alex-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The charity itself works to prevent the effects of drug and alcohol misuse on young people and it also aims to support, inform and inspire vulnerable and disadvantaged young people to help them reach their full potential.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> On 12 March 2013, with the help of ex-addict <a href="/wiki/Russell_Brand" title="Russell Brand">Russell Brand</a>, the Foundation launched the Amy Winehouse Foundation Resilience Programme For Schools across the UK which aims to provide effective education around drugs, alcohol and dealing with emotional issues.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films">Films</span></h3>\n<p>A documentary film, <i><a href="/wiki/Amy_(2015_film)" title="Amy (2015 film)">Amy</a></i> (2015), directed by <a href="/wiki/Asif_Kapadia" title="Asif Kapadia">Asif Kapadia</a>, was released in the United Kingdom on 3 July and worldwide on 10 July. The film attempts to portray Winehouse as a "Fragile Jewish girl" who had a great music talent but unfortunately became a victim to her addictions and eating disorder, while people who should have helped her did not.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> The film received its premi\xc3\xa8re at the <a href="/wiki/2015_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2015 Cannes Film Festival">2015 Cannes Film Festival</a> on 16 May and has been reviewed as "a tragic masterpiece", "brilliant", "heartbreaking" and "unmissable".<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Amy_(soundtrack)" title="Amy (soundtrack)">soundtrack of the same name</a> was released on 30 October 2015, along with the DVD that includes music featured in the documentary by film composer <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B4nio_Pinto_(composer)" title="Ant\xc3\xb4nio Pinto (composer)">Ant\xc3\xb4nio Pinto</a> and classic tracks by Winehouse.\n</p><p>The film has received various accolades, including the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Documentary_Feature" title="Academy Award for Best Documentary Feature">Academy Award for Best Documentary Feature</a> at the <a href="/wiki/88th_Academy_Awards" title="88th Academy Awards">2016 Oscars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Music_Film" title="Grammy Award for Best Music Film">Best Music Film</a> at the <a href="/wiki/58th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="58th Annual Grammy Awards">2016 Grammy Awards</a>, the <a href="/wiki/69th_British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="69th British Academy Film Awards">BAFTA</a> for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Documentary" title="BAFTA Award for Best Documentary">Best Documentary</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2016_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2016 MTV Movie Awards">MTV Movie Award</a> for Best Documentary, in addition to a nomination for the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_British_Film" title="BAFTA Award for Best British Film">BAFTA Award for Best British Film</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> The success of the film has also led Winehouse her second posthumous nomination for Best British Female Solo Artist at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Brit_Awards" title="2016 Brit Awards">2016 Brit Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 November 2015, it was announced that a new drama biopic about Winehouse\'s life simply entitled as <i>Amy Winehouse</i> is in production, directed and written by <a href="/wiki/Kirsten_Sheridan" title="Kirsten Sheridan">Kirsten Sheridan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> It was also revealed that actress <a href="/wiki/Noomi_Rapace" title="Noomi Rapace">Noomi Rapace</a> is in talks to star as Winehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>\n<p>Although Winehouse was raised Jewish and expressed pride in being Jewish, she was not religious.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> During one interview, Winehouse said "being Jewish to me is about being together as a real family. It\xe2\x80\x99s not about lighting candles and saying a bracha."<sup id="cite_ref-amyw1_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amyw1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse also frequently performed with a large <a href="/wiki/Star_of_David" title="Star of David">Star of David</a> medallion.<sup id="cite_ref-amyw1_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amyw1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, in memory of Winehouse the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_London" title="Jewish Museum London">Jewish Museum London</a> ran an exhibition titled "Amy Winehouse: A Family Portrait".<sup id="cite_ref-amyw1_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amyw1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The museum researched about her paternal great-great-grandfather\xe2\x80\x99s arrival from <a href="/wiki/Minsk" title="Minsk">Minsk</a> in 1890, and how the family finally settled in London, starting out in working-class jobs before gradually moving to middle-class jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-amyw1_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amyw1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse had 14 known tattoos, including "Daddy\'s Girl" on her left arm for her father and the name "Cynthia" on her right arm in memory of her Jewish grandmother.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships">Relationships</span></h3>\n<p>Winehouse dated chef-musician <a href="/wiki/Alex_Clare" title="Alex Clare">Alex Clare</a> (sometimes referred to as Alex Claire) in 2006, while on a break from her on-off boyfriend and future husband, Blake Fielder-Civil. She and Clare lived together briefly,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201262_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse201262-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> and in a pattern that Fielder-Civil would later repeat, Clare famously sold his story to the <i><a href="/wiki/News_of_the_World" title="News of the World">News of the World</a></i>, which published it under the headline "Bondage Crazed Amy Just Can\'t Beehive in Bed."<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fielder-Civil (born August 1978), a former video production assistant,<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!_News_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!_News-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> had dropped out of <a href="/wiki/Bourne_Grammar_School" title="Bourne Grammar School">Bourne Grammar School</a> and, aged 16, moved to London from his native <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In a June 2007 interview, Winehouse admitted she could sometimes be violent toward him after she had been drinking, saying: "If he says one thing I don\'t like, then I\'ll chin him."<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> In August 2007, they were photographed, bloodied and bruised, in the streets of London after an alleged fight, although she contended her injuries were self-inflicted.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse married Fielder-Civil on 18 May 2007, in <a href="/wiki/Miami_Beach,_Florida" title="Miami Beach, Florida">Miami Beach, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Yahoo!_News_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yahoo!_News-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse\'s parents and in-laws publicly reported their numerous concerns, the latter citing fears that the two might commit suicide. Fielder-Civil\'s father encouraged fans to boycott Winehouse\'s music, and Mitch Winehouse said this would not help.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> Fielder-Civil was quoted in a British tabloid as saying he introduced Winehouse to <a href="/wiki/Crack_cocaine" title="Crack cocaine">crack cocaine</a> and heroin.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> During a visit with Mitch Winehouse at the prison in July 2008, Fielder-Civil reportedly said that he and Winehouse would cut themselves to ease the pain of <a href="/wiki/Drug_withdrawal" title="Drug withdrawal">withdrawal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 21 July 2008 to 25 February 2009, Fielder-Civil was imprisoned following his guilty plea on charges of trying to <a href="/wiki/Perverting_the_course_of_justice" title="Perverting the course of justice">pervert the course of justice</a> and of grievous bodily harm with intent.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> The incident, in July 2007, involved his assault of a pub landlord that broke the victim\'s cheek.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> According to the prosecution, the landlord accepted \xc2\xa3200,000 as part of a deal to "effectively throw the [court] case and not turn up," and he testified that the money belonged to Winehouse,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> but she pulled out of a meeting with the men involved in the plot, to attend an awards ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Mitch Winehouse, as manager of his daughter\'s money, has denied the payoff came from her.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When Winehouse was spotted with aspiring actor <a href="/wiki/Josh_Bowman" title="Josh Bowman">Josh Bowman</a> on holiday in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, in early January 2009, she said she was "in love again, and I don\'t need drugs."<sup id="cite_ref-lucia_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lucia-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> She commented that her "whole marriage was based on doing drugs" and that "for the time being I\'ve just forgotten I\'m even married."<sup id="cite_ref-lucia_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lucia-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> On 12 January, Winehouse\'s spokesman confirmed that "papers have been received" for what Fielder-Civil\'s solicitor has said are divorce proceedings based on a claim of adultery.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> In March, Winehouse was quoted in a magazine as saying, "I still love Blake and I want him to move into my new house with me\xe2\x80\x94that was my plan all along ... I won\'t let him divorce me. He\'s the male version of me and we\'re perfect for each other."<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, an uncontested divorce was granted on 16 July 2009 and became final on 28 August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> Fielder-Civil received no money in the settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-Mitch_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mitch-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Winehouse\'s death, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Doherty" title="Pete Doherty">Pete Doherty</a> said that he and Winehouse had been lovers at one point. Speaking to the <i>Daily Mail</i> about it he said "This is difficult for me to admit. But, yes, it\'s true. Amy and I were lovers. I loved her then and, well, I still do today. But towards the end, as only lovers can, she became quite mean and cruel to me. She didn\'t suffer fools\xe2\x80\xa6and believe me, she had a mean right hook."<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> However, in July 2008, when <i>Rolling Stone</i> reporter Claire Hoffman asked Winehouse about her relationship with Doherty, Winehouse replied: "We\'re just good friends", and added: "I asked Pete to do a concept EP, and he made this face, he looked at me like I\'d pooed on the floor. He wouldn\'t do it. We\'re just really close".<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Substance_abuse_and_mental_illness">Substance abuse and mental illness</span></h3>\n<p>Winehouse\'s battles with <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">substance abuse</a> were the subject of much media attention. In 2005, she went through a period of drinking, heavy drug use, and weight loss.<sup id="cite_ref-Mitch_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mitch-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RS_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> People who saw her during the end of that year and early 2006 reported a rebound that coincided with the writing of <i>Back to Black</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Her family believes that the mid-2006 death of her grandmother, who was a stabilising influence, set her off into addiction.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_27-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In August 2007, Winehouse cancelled a number of shows in the UK and Europe, citing exhaustion and ill health. She was hospitalised during this period for what was reported as an <a href="/wiki/Drug_overdose" title="Drug overdose">overdose</a> of heroin, <a href="/wiki/MDMA" title="MDMA">ecstasy</a>, cocaine, <a href="/wiki/Ketamine" title="Ketamine">ketamine</a> and alcohol.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> In various interviews, she admitted to having problems with <a href="/wiki/Self-harm" title="Self-harm">self-harm</a>, depression, and <a href="/wiki/Eating_disorder" title="Eating disorder">eating disorders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DD_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DD-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Profile_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Profile-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse told a magazine that the drugs were to blame for her hospitalisation and that "I really thought that it was over for me then."<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Soon afterward, Winehouse\'s father commented that when he had made public statements regarding her problems he was using the media because it seemed the only way to get through to her.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Album_Chart_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="The Album Chart Show">The Album Chart Show</a></i> on British television, Winehouse said she was <a href="/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">manic depressive</a> and not alcoholic, adding that that sounded like "an alcoholic in denial."<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> A US reporter writes that Winehouse was a "victim of mental illness in a society that doesn\'t understand or respond to mental illness with great effectiveness."<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2007, Winehouse\'s spokesman reported that the singer was in a physician-supervised programme and was channelling her difficulties by writing a lot of music.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> The British tabloid <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun</a></i> posted a video of a woman, alleged to be Winehouse, apparently smoking crack cocaine and speaking of having taken ecstasy and <a href="/wiki/Valium" class="mw-redirect" title="Valium">valium</a>. Winehouse\'s father moved in with her,<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Island_Records" title="Island Records">Island Records</a>, her record label, announced the abandonment of plans for an American promotion campaign on her behalf.<sup id="cite_ref-jan24_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jan24-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> In late January 2008, Winehouse reportedly entered a rehabilitation facility for a two-week treatment program.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 23 January 2008, the video was passed on to the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Police">Metropolitan Police</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-jan24_164-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jan24-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> who questioned her on 5 February.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> No charges were brought. On 26 March 2008, Winehouse\'s spokesman said she was "doing well."<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> Her record company reportedly believed that her recovery remained fragile.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> By late April 2008, her erratic behaviour, including an allegation of assault, caused fear that her drug rehabilitation efforts had been unsuccessful,<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> leading to efforts by Winehouse\'s father and manager to seek assistance in having her <a href="/wiki/Involuntary_commitment#United_Kingdom" title="Involuntary commitment">detained under the Mental Health Act 1983</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> Her dishevelled appearance during and after a scheduled club night in September sparked new rumours of a relapse. Photographers were quoted as saying she appeared to have cuts on her legs and arms.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to her physician, Winehouse quit illegal substances in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-coronor_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coronor-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> In an October 2010 interview, speaking of her decision to quit drugs, Winehouse said, "I literally woke up one day and was like, \'I don\'t want to do this any more\'."<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> Drinking alcohol emerged as a problem with Winehouse abstaining for a few weeks then lapsing.<sup id="cite_ref-coronor_265-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coronor-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> The physician said that Winehouse was treated with <a href="/wiki/Chlordiazepoxide" title="Chlordiazepoxide">Librium</a> for <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_withdrawal" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcohol withdrawal">alcohol withdrawal</a> and anxiety, and underwent psychological and psychiatric evaluations in 2010, but refused psychological therapy.<sup id="cite_ref-coronor_265-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coronor-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Violence_and_legal_difficulties">Violence and legal difficulties</span></h3>\n<p>In 2006, Winehouse admitted to punching a female fan in the face for criticising her having taken Blake Fielder-Civil as a husband. She then attacked her own spouse as he attempted to calm her down.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> In October 2007, Winehouse and Fielder-Civil were arrested in <a href="/wiki/Bergen" title="Bergen">Bergen</a>, Norway, for possession of seven grams of <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a>. The couple were later released and fined 3850 <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_krone" title="Norwegian krone">kroner</a> (around \xc2\xa3350).<sup id="cite_ref-summoned_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-summoned-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse first appealed the fines,<sup id="cite_ref-summoned_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-summoned-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> but later dropped the appeal.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 April 2008, Winehouse was <a href="/wiki/Police_caution" title="Police caution">cautioned</a> after she admitted to police she slapped a 38-year-old man in the face, a "<a href="/wiki/Common_assault" title="Common assault">common assault</a>" offence, her first of two. She voluntarily turned herself in and was held overnight. Police said, at her arrival she was "in no fit state" to be interviewed.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> Ten days later, Winehouse was arrested on suspicion of possessing drugs after a video of her apparently smoking crack cocaine was passed to the police in January, but was released on bail a few hours later because they could not confirm, from the video, what she was smoking.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> The Crown Prosecution Service considered charging her, but cleared her when it could not establish that the substance in the video was a controlled drug.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Some members of <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament</a> reacted negatively.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> Two London residents were subsequently charged with <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_(criminal)" title="Conspiracy (criminal)">conspiracy</a> to supply cocaine and ecstasy to Winehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> One of the pair was sentenced to two years in prison on 13 December 2008, while the other received a two-year community order.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 March 2009, Winehouse was arrested and charged with common assault following a claim by Sharene Flash that Winehouse hit her in the eye at the September 2008 Prince\'s Trust charity ball.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse\'s spokesperson announced the cancellation of the singer\'s US <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella Festival</a> appearance in light of the new legal issue,<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> and Winehouse appeared in court on 17 March to enter her plea of not guilty.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> On 23 July, her trial began with prosecutor Lyall Thompson charging that Winehouse acted with "deliberate and unjustifiable violence" while appearing to be under the influence of alcohol or another substance. She testified that she did not punch Flash, but tried to push her away because she was scared of her; she cited her worry that Flash would sell her story to a tabloid, Flash\'s height advantage, and Flash\'s "rude" behaviour.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> On 24 July, District Judge <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Workman" title="Timothy Workman">Timothy Workman</a> ruled that Winehouse was not guilty, citing the facts that all but two of the witnesses were intoxicated at the time of the incident and that medical evidence did not show "the sort of injury that often occurs when there is a forceful punch to the eye."<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 December 2009, Winehouse was arrested for a third time on charges of common assault, plus another charge of <a href="/wiki/Public_Order_Act_1986" title="Public Order Act 1986">public order offence</a> after assaulting the front-of-house manager of the <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Theatre" title="Milton Keynes Theatre">Milton Keynes Theatre</a> after he asked her to move from her seat.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse plead guilty to the charges and was given a conditional discharge.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paparazzi">Paparazzi</span></h3>\n<p>With the <a href="/wiki/Paparazzi" title="Paparazzi">paparazzi</a> taking photographs of her wherever they could, Winehouse obtained an <a href="/wiki/Injunction" title="Injunction">injunction</a> against a leading paparazzi agency, Big Pictures, under the <a href="/wiki/Protection_from_Harassment_Act_1997" title="Protection from Harassment Act 1997">Protection from Harassment Act 1997</a>; the resultant court order issued by the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court</a> in 2009 banned them from following her.<sup id="cite_ref-paparazzi_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paparazzi-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Photographers were also banned from following her within 100 metres of her London home and photographing Winehouse in her home or the homes of her friends and relatives. According to a newspaper report, sources close to the singer said legal action was taken out of concern for the safety of Winehouse and those close to her.<sup id="cite_ref-paparazzi_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paparazzi-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Respiratory_and_other_health_problems">Respiratory and other health problems</span></h3>\n<p>On 23 June 2008, Winehouse\'s publicist corrected earlier misstatements by Mitch Winehouse that his daughter had early stage <a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">emphysema</a>, instead claiming she had signs of what could lead to early-stage emphysema.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Mitch Winehouse had also stated that his daughter\'s <a href="/wiki/Lung_volumes" title="Lung volumes">lungs were operating at 70 percent capacity</a> and that she had an <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_dysrhythmia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardiac dysrhythmia">irregular heartbeat</a>. He said that these problems had been caused by her <a href="/wiki/Chain_smoking" title="Chain smoking">chain smoking</a> crack cocaine. The singer\'s father also reported that doctors had warned Winehouse that, if she continued smoking <a href="/wiki/Crack_cocaine" title="Crack cocaine">crack cocaine</a>, she would have to wear an <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_mask" title="Oxygen mask">oxygen mask</a> and would eventually die.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> In a radio interview, Mitch Winehouse said the singer was responding "fabulously" to treatment, which included being covered with <a href="/wiki/Nicotine_patch" title="Nicotine patch">nicotine patches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> British Lung Foundation spokesman Keith Prowse noted this type of condition could be managed with treatment. Prowse also said the condition was not normal for a person her age but "heavy smoking and inhaling other substances like drugs can age the lungs prematurely."<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Norman H. Edelman of the <a href="/wiki/American_Lung_Association" title="American Lung Association">American Lung Association</a> explained that if she stopped smoking, her lung functions would decline at the rate of a normal person, but continued smoking would lead to a more rapid decline in lung function.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse was released from the <a href="/wiki/London_Clinic" class="mw-redirect" title="London Clinic">London Clinic</a> 24 hours after returning from a temporary leave to perform at <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela" title="Nelson Mandela">Nelson Mandela</a>\'s 90th birthday and at a concert in Glastonbury, and continued receiving treatment as an <a href="/wiki/Outpatient" class="mw-redirect" title="Outpatient">outpatient</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> In July 2008, Winehouse stated that she had been diagnosed with "some areas of emphysema" and said she was getting herself together by "eating loads of healthy food, sleeping loads, playing my guitar, making music and writing letters to my husband every day."<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> She also kept a vertical <a href="/wiki/Tanning_bed" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanning bed">tanning bed</a> in her flat.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoffman_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoffman-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse began precautionary testing on her lungs and chest on 25 October 2008<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> at the London Clinic for what was reported as a chest infection. Winehouse was in and out of the facility and was granted permission to set her own schedule regarding home leave.<sup id="cite_ref-Nov_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nov-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> She returned to the hospital on 23 November 2008 for a reported reaction to her medication.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_Memorial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Amy_Winehouse_Memorial.jpg/170px-Amy_Winehouse_Memorial.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Amy_Winehouse_Memorial.jpg/255px-Amy_Winehouse_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Amy_Winehouse_Memorial.jpg/340px-Amy_Winehouse_Memorial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="3072" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy_Winehouse_Memorial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tributes outside Amy Winehouse\'s home at <a href="/wiki/Camden_Square" title="Camden Square">Camden Square</a> days following her death on 23 July 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>Winehouse\'s bodyguard said that he had arrived at her residence three days before her death and felt she had been somewhat intoxicated. He observed moderate drinking over the next few days. He observed her "laughing, listening to music and watching TV at 2 a.m. the day of her death". According to the bodyguard, at 10 a.m. he observed her lying on her bed and tried unsuccessfully to rouse her. This did not raise much suspicion because she usually slept late after a night out. According to the bodyguard, shortly after 3<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>p.m., he checked on her again and observed her lying in the same position as before, leading to a further check, in which he concluded that she was not breathing and had no pulse. He said he subsequently called emergency services.<sup id="cite_ref-coronor_265-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coronor-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At 3:54<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>p.m. <a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">BST</a> on 23 July 2011, two ambulances were called to Winehouse\'s home in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Camden" title="London Borough of Camden">Camden</a>, London.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse was pronounced dead at the scene. Shortly afterwards, the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Service" title="Metropolitan Police Service">Metropolitan Police</a> confirmed that she had died.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> After her death was announced, media and camera crews appeared, as crowds gathered near Winehouse\'s residence to pay their respects. <a href="/wiki/Forensic_science" title="Forensic science">Forensic</a> investigators entered the flat as police cordoned off the street outside; they recovered one small and two large bottles of vodka from her room.<sup id="cite_ref-coronor_265-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coronor-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> After her death, the singer broke her second Guinness World Record: for the most songs by a woman to simultaneously appear on the UK singles chart, with eight.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A coroner\'s <a href="/wiki/Inquest" title="Inquest">inquest</a> reached a verdict of <a href="/wiki/Death_by_misadventure#Verdict" title="Death by misadventure">misadventure</a>. The report released on 26 October 2011 explained that Winehouse\'s <a href="/wiki/Blood_alcohol_content" title="Blood alcohol content">blood alcohol content</a> was 416<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><span title="milligrams">mg</span> per 100<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span><span title="milliliters">ml</span> (0.416%) at the time of her death, more than five times <a href="/wiki/Drunk_driving_law_by_country#United_Kingdom" title="Drunk driving law by country">the legal drink-drive limit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coronor_265-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coronor-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> According to the coroner, "The unintended consequences of such potentially fatal levels was her sudden death."<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy-Winehouse-Tribute-Concert-Bucharest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Amy-Winehouse-Tribute-Concert-Bucharest.jpg/220px-Amy-Winehouse-Tribute-Concert-Bucharest.jpg" width="220" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Amy-Winehouse-Tribute-Concert-Bucharest.jpg/330px-Amy-Winehouse-Tribute-Concert-Bucharest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Amy-Winehouse-Tribute-Concert-Bucharest.jpg/440px-Amy-Winehouse-Tribute-Concert-Bucharest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="1388" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amy-Winehouse-Tribute-Concert-Bucharest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Romanian singers <a href="/wiki/Rona_Hartner" title="Rona Hartner">Rona Hartner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paula_Seling" title="Paula Seling">Paula Seling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nico_(Romanian_singer)" title="Nico (Romanian singer)">Nico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maria_Radu" title="Maria Radu">Maria Radu</a> performing at a memorial Amy Winehouse concert in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> on 23 October 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>Winehouse\'s record label, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Republic_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Republic Records">Universal Republic</a>, released a statement that read in part: "We are deeply saddened at the sudden loss of such a gifted musician, artist and performer."<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> Many musical artists have since paid tribute to Winehouse including <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>, <a href="/wiki/M.I.A._(rapper)" title="M.I.A. (rapper)">M.I.A.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marianne_Faithfull" title="Marianne Faithfull">Marianne Faithfull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Mars" title="Bruno Mars">Bruno Mars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keisha_Buchanan" title="Keisha Buchanan">Keisha Buchanan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Courtney_Love" title="Courtney Love">Courtney Love</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> and the punk rock band <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a>, who wrote a song in her tribute titled "Amy".<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> In her 2012 album <i><a href="/wiki/Banga_(album)" title="Banga (album)">Banga</a></i>, singer <a href="/wiki/Patti_Smith" title="Patti Smith">Patti Smith</a> released "This Is the Girl," written as a homage to Winehouse.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Ronson" title="Mark Ronson">Mark Ronson</a> dedicated his UK number one album <i><a href="/wiki/Uptown_Special" title="Uptown Special">Uptown Special</a></i> to Winehouse, stating: "I\'m always thinking of you and inspired by you."<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> There was a large amount of media attention devoted to the <a href="/wiki/27_Club" title="27 Club">27 Club</a> once again.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> Three years earlier, she had expressed a fear of dying at that age.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Family and friends attended Winehouse\'s funeral on 26 July 2011 at <a href="/wiki/Jewish_cemeteries_in_London" title="Jewish cemeteries in London">Edgwarebury Lane cemetery</a> in north London.<sup id="cite_ref-TimeFuneral_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimeFuneral-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCFuneral_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCFuneral-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> Her mother and father, Janis and Mitch Winehouse, close friend <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Osbourne" title="Kelly Osbourne">Kelly Osbourne</a>, producer Mark Ronson, and her boyfriend Reg Traviss were among those in attendance at the private service led by Rabbi Frank Hellner.<sup id="cite_ref-TimeFuneral_306-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimeFuneral-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCFuneral_307-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCFuneral-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> Her father delivered the eulogy, saying "Goodnight, my angel, sleep tight. Mummy and Daddy love you ever so much."<sup id="cite_ref-TimeFuneral_306-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TimeFuneral-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> Carole King\'s "<a href="/wiki/So_Far_Away_(Carole_King_song)" title="So Far Away (Carole King song)">So Far Away</a>" closed the service with mourners singing along.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> She was later <a href="/wiki/Cremation" title="Cremation">cremated</a> at <a href="/wiki/Golders_Green_Crematorium" title="Golders Green Crematorium">Golders Green Crematorium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Marikar_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marikar-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> The family planned to sit a two-day <a href="/wiki/Shiva_(Judaism)" title="Shiva (Judaism)">shiva</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Marikar_310-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marikar-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse\'s parents set up The Amy Winehouse Foundation to prevent harm from drug misuse among young people, and Amy Winehouse\'s brother Alex is an employee.<sup id="cite_ref-Alex_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alex-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> Winehouse did not leave a will; her estate was inherited by her parents.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 December 2012, British authorities reopened the probe of Winehouse\'s death.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> On 8 January 2013, a second inquest confirmed that Winehouse died of accidental alcohol poisoning.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> In a late June 2013 interview, Alex Winehouse revealed his belief that his sister\'s eating disorder, and the consequent physical weakness, was the primary cause of her death:\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>She suffered from <a href="/wiki/Bulimia_nervosa" title="Bulimia nervosa">bulimia</a> very badly. That\'s not, like, a revelation \xe2\x80\x93 you knew just by looking at her\xe2\x80\xa6 She would have died eventually, the way she was going, but what really killed her was the bulimia\xe2\x80\xa6 I think that it left her weaker and more susceptible. Had she not had an eating disorder, she would have been physically stronger.<sup id="cite_ref-Alex_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alex-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Posthumous_retrospectives">Posthumous retrospectives</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:27_club_Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/27_club_Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv.jpg/220px-27_club_Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/27_club_Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv.jpg/330px-27_club_Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/27_club_Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv.jpg/440px-27_club_Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:27_club_Graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/27_Club_graffiti_in_Tel_Aviv" title="27 Club graffiti in Tel Aviv">27 Club graffiti in Tel Aviv</a> depicting Winehouse as a key figure</div></div></div>\n<p>Winehouse\'s parents have each written memoirs about their daughter and donated the proceeds from both books to the <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse_Foundation" title="Amy Winehouse Foundation">Amy Winehouse Foundation</a>. In the introduction to Mitch Winehouse\'s biography, entitled <i>Amy: My Daughter</i> (2012), he explained: "Apart from being her father, I was also her friend, confidant and adviser\xe2\x80\x94not that she always took my advice, but she always heard me out."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012ix_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinehouse2012ix-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> Her mother Janis published <i>Loving Amy: A Mother\'s Story</i>, in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Winehouse is the subject of <i><a href="/wiki/Amy_(2015_film)" title="Amy (2015 film)">Amy</a></i> (2015), a documentary directed by <a href="/wiki/Asif_Kapadia" title="Asif Kapadia">Asif Kapadia</a> and produced by <a href="/wiki/James_Gay-Rees" title="James Gay-Rees">James Gay-Rees</a>, Kapadia, and Universal Music.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> Kapadia and Gay-Rees introduced the project at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival" title="Cannes Film Festival">Cannes Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> The film debuted at the 2015 Cannes Film Festival<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> and won the 2016 Academy Award for Best Documentary Feature.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An exhibit of Winehouse\'s personal items, co-curated by her brother and sister-in-law, entitled <i>Amy Winehouse: A Family Portrait</i>, was on display at the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Museum_London" title="Jewish Museum London">Jewish Museum London</a> from 3 July 2013 until 15 September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> Display items, such as books and music, were featured together with captions written by Winehouse\'s brother.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late 2011, there were reports that Winehouse\'s former boyfriend, Reg Traviss, was developing a film about her. Winehouse\'s father Mitch Winehouse, who owns the copyright to his daughter\'s music, said he would not authorise the use of her music for the film.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse_discography" title="Amy Winehouse discography">Amy Winehouse discography</a></div>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Frank_(Amy_Winehouse_album)" title="Frank (Amy Winehouse album)">Frank</a></i> (2003)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_Black" title="Back to Black">Back to Black</a></i> (2006)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography">Filmography</span></h2>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Amy_(2015_film)" title="Amy (2015 film)">Amy</a></i> (2015)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Caulfield, Keith (23 July 2012). <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130127232308/http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/480976/amy-winehouses-death-led-to-surge-in-sales-chart-moves">"Amy Winehouse\'s Death Led to Surge in Sales, Chart Moves"</a>.
